                           <msub>
                              <mi>D</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>a</mi>
                                 <mi>p</mi>
                                 <mi>p</mi>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <mfrac>
                              <msup>
                                 <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                    <mrow>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>z</mi>
                                          <mi>c</mi>
                                       </msub>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>c</mi>
                                          <mn>0</mn>
                                       </msub>
                                       <mi>F</mi>
                                    </mrow>
                                 </mfenced>
                                 <mn>2</mn>
                              </msup>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mn>4</mn>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>J</mi>
                                          <msub>
                                             <mi>t</mi>
                                             <mi>a</mi>
                                          </msub>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </mfenced>
                                    <mn>2</mn>
                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                           </mfrac>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{t}_{Sand}} = \pi {{D}_{app}}\frac{{{{{\left( {{{z}_c}{{c}_0}F} \right)}}^2}}}{{4{{{\left( {J{{t}_a}} \right)}}^2}}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>where z<sub>c</sub> is the charge number of the cation (z<sub>c</sub> = 1 for Na<sup>+</sup>), c<sub>0</sub> is the bulk salt concentration, F is the Faraday's constant, J is the current density, and t<sub>a</sub> = 1– t<sub>Na</sub> is the transference number of anions. It can be seen that the high cation transference number and low anion transference number would effectively prolong dendrite nucleation time and thus suppressing sodium dendrite formation. The cation transference number of the cell with Zn-diamane/PP separator is as high as 0.66, implying that the Zn-diamane/PP separator could accelerate the cation migration and simultaneously restricting anion mobility, thereby suppressing the dendrite nucleation and proliferation of dendrites. Furthermore, the Na<sup>+</sup> ion conductivity (σ) through different separators is calculated from the EIS according to:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0072" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0072_R_d5601348e1081" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 72 - Energy Storage Mater.">72</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202417809-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/26122f8f-5f59-4eaa-9484-335989bf48a5/adfm202417809-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202417809:adfm202417809-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202417809-math-0002.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>σ</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mfrac>
                              <mi>D</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>R</mi>
                                 <mi>S</mi>
                              </mrow>
                           </mfrac>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}\sigma = \frac{D}{{RS}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>where D and S denote the thickness and area of the separator respectively, and R denotes the resistance of the electrolyte obtained from the EIS analysis. The Zn-diamane/PP separator exhibits a superior σ of 1.89 to the 0.49 mS cm<sup>−1</sup> for PP and 0.93 mS cm<sup>−1</sup> for diamane/PP separator (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0003">3g,h</a>). This ionic conductivity is also higher than the reported Na ionic conductivities achieved by other separators, such as Co-NWS (1.39 mS cm<sup>−1</sup>), porous ZIF-based membrane (PZM) (1.54 mS cm<sup>−1</sup>), cellulose-based composite separator (CP@PPC) (0.69 mS cm<sup>−1</sup>), S-3500 (1.47 mS cm<sup>−1</sup>), and NASICON-type fast ionic conductor layer (NZSP@PP) (0.96 mS cm<sup>−1</sup>), demonstrating the advantage of Zn-diamane/PP separator for accelerating the Na ion migration speed (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0041_R_d5601348e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Mater.">41</a>, <a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0045_R_d5601348e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">45</a>, <a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0065_R_d5601348e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Adv. Mater.">65</a>, <a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0073" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0073_R_d5601348e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 73 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">73</a>, <a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0074" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0074_R_d5601348e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 74 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">74</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></div>
         
         <p>To deep understanding the mechanisms underlying the improved electrochemical performance, a detailed investigation was conducted into the rectification effects of the Zn-diamane/PP separators on Na ion flux, such as deposition morphology evolution of the anodes, ion flux concentration, interface phase change, and SEI layer compositions. The Na electrode morphologies were examined from the macro-scale by dissembling the Na||Na symmetric cells with the PP, diamane/PP, and Zn-diamane/PP separators after 10 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> as shown <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4a</a>. The surface of the cycled Na foil from the cell with the PP separator is rough even porous morphology (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4a</a>, up image), while the Na foil with the diamane/PP separator exhibits a flat surface with non-porous morphology (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4a</a>, middle image). In contrast, the Na foil from the cell with the Zn-diamane/PP separator exhibits flat and smooth morphology (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4a</a>, bottom image). To visualize and compare the effect of modulated separators on dendrite suppression, Na metal deposition morphology evolution from the side view with various separators at the submillimeter scale was investigated by in situ optical microscopy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4b–d</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information). As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, when measured at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>, Na pinpoints are shown in the cell with a PP separator just after 30 mins of deposition, and these pinpoints grow into dendrites larger and larger after 60 mins of deposition. In contrast, the Na deposition surface always keeps smooth deposition morphology in the cell with diamane/PP and Zn-diamane/PP separator during the 120 mins of deposition. Although the cell with diamane/PP separator can maintain the dendrite-free deposition morphology at a low current density, dendrite formation is still observed at higher current densities and larger areal capacities, such as 4 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 8 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4b–d</a>, plenty of sharp dendrites are exhibited in the cell with PP and diamane/PP separators after only 10 mins of deposition, and these dendrites are grown into giant mossy-like dendrites by 120 mins (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4b,c</a>). In contrast, homogeneous Na metals are deposited on the Na metal anodes surface of the cell with Zn-diamane/PP separators with dendrite-free morphology during the 120 mins of deposition at a high current density of 4 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4d</a>). These findings indicate that the diamane can inhibit the dendrite formation at mild testing conditions (≈1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 2 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>), higher sodiophilic interface is essential for guiding Na metal deposition at an elevated current density and areal capacity (4 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 8 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0075" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0075_R_d5601348e1187" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">75</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition to investigating the surface deposition morphology from the sub-millimeter scale, the deposition morphology evolution from the micro-meter scale was also investigated by ex-situ SEM characterization. As seen in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4e–g</a>, compared with Na metal anodes with PP separator and diamane/PP separator after 10 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, Na metal anode with Zn-diamane/PP separator shows the flattest surface without any presence of protrusions and cracks, which is agreed well with the in situ optical microscopy results. Similar results are more prominent at high current and large areal capacity (for example, 5 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 10 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>), Na foil from the cell with the Zn-diamane/PP separator also exhibits the flattest and most smooth morphology compared with the control samples (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417809-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9cc11842-111c-4830-9013-b8563add7367/adfm202417809-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9cc11842-111c-4830-9013-b8563add7367/adfm202417809-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/af16358c-6773-4576-a463-b39f4bca2314/adfm202417809-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9cc11842-111c-4830-9013-b8563add7367/adfm202417809-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417809-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417809" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Mechanism investigation of the Na deposition behavior induced by the modified separators. a) Digital photos of the Na deposition morphologies on the surface of the Na metals in the Na||Na symmetric cells with the PP (up), diamane/PP (middle) and Zn-diamane/PP (bottom) separators after 10 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. In situ optical microscopy characterization of the morphology evolution of Na deposition on Na metal in Na||Na symmetric cells with b) PP c) diamane/PP and d) Zn-diamane/PP separators at 4 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>. SEM images of the Na electrodes with e) PP, f) diamane/PP, and g) Zn-diamane/PP separators after 10 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. Na ion distribution simulation of the Na<sup>+</sup> ions through h) PP, i) diamane/PP, and j) Zn-diamane/PP separators.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In addition to the morphology evolution, the ion flux concentration across the employed separators was simulated by COMSOL Multiphysics (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4h–j</a>). The results show that the local current density at the macropores of the PP separators is much higher than that at the adjacent areas between two macropores. These uneven Na ion flux originating from the inhomogeneous macropores in PP separators generate “hot spots” beneath the macropores. During the electroplating process, a large amount of Na ions are accumulated at these hot spots, leading to irregular Na metal nucleated onto the pinpoints and growing into large dendrites (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4h</a>). On the contrary, the diamane layer and Zn NPs layer on the surface of the PP separator can effectively rectify the Na ion flux into a much lower local current density and more homogeneous dispersive distribution beneath the macropores modulated by the Zn-diamane layer (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0004">4i,j</a>). These results prove that the Na ions are uniformly distributed through the rectified by Zn-diamane/PP separators and the sodiophilicity of the Zn NPs, which can effectively guide the Na ion deposition with a dendrite-free morphology.</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">From the top-view image of the Na electrode after cycling and the EDS elemental mapping images shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5a</a>, there is no Zn element distributed on the surface of the Na electrode. However, the Zn and Na elements are found on the surface of the Zn-diamane/PP separator (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5b</a>). Cross-sectional SEM images and corresponding element distributions show that Na distribution is consistent with that of Zn with a thickness of ≈2&nbsp;µm (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information). This is due to the formation of NaZn<sub>13</sub> alloy, which is in situ formed on the separator surface after the discharge process (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5c</a>). The corresponding electrochemical reaction is:

            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202417809-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/07b1bf31-1809-4e59-880a-20fb50d8b401/adfm202417809-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202417809:adfm202417809-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202417809-math-0003.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>Na</mi>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           </mrow>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">+</mo>
                           <mn>13</mn>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>Zn</mi>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           </mrow>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">=</mo>
                           <mrow>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                              <mi>NaZ</mi>
                           </mrow>
                           <msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi>
                              <mn>13</mn>
                           </msub>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm{Na\ }} + 13{\mathrm{Zn\ }} = {\mathrm{\ NaZ}}{{{\mathrm{n}}}_{13}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417809-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c5071c79-4266-40de-9b71-ce7d249be575/adfm202417809-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/c5071c79-4266-40de-9b71-ce7d249be575/adfm202417809-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/03251595-ad8b-4e1e-bf76-d63d49e89c9b/adfm202417809-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c5071c79-4266-40de-9b71-ce7d249be575/adfm202417809-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417809-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417809" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Characterization of the surface chemistry of the Na metal anode and Zn-diamane/PP. a) Optical photographs of the Na metal anode and b) Zn-diamane/PP separator disassembled from the Na||Na symmetric cell after 10 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, and corresponding elemental distribution of Na and Zn. c) XRD of the Zn-diamane/PP separator surface after 10 cycles&nbsp;at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. d) Binding energy between Na<sup>+</sup> ions and NaZn<sub>13</sub> alloy calculated by DFT. e) Na deposition dynamics upon the Zn surface simulated by AIMD calculation within 50 ps. XPS depth profiling of f) C 1s, g) O 1s, and h) F 1s elemental distribution analysis of the surface of Na anode after 30 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. i)&nbsp;Schematic illustration of the modulated Zn-diamane/PP separators to enhance the electrochemical performance of Na metal anodes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>DFT calculation shows that the binding energy between Na ions and NaZn<sub>13</sub> is as high as −1.74 eV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5d</a>), which is higher than that of Na ions with (110) crystal plane of diamane (−0.81 eV) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a>, Supporting Information). Furthermore, the ab initio molecular dynamics (AIMD) approach was utilized to elucidate Na deposition chemistry on the surface of Zn NPs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5e</a>). The findings indicate a propensity for Na to be absorbed onto the Zn substrate, followed by forming a dense Na–Zn alloy phase. The elevated interaction between Na ions and the in situ formed NaZn<sub>13</sub> facilitates the effective absorption and redistribution of the Na ions, leading to a homogeneous ion distribution since the formed NaZn<sub>13</sub> alloy NPs are uniformly distributed over the modulated separators. This result demonstrates that the sodiophilicity of the modulated Zn-diamane/PP separator is due to the formation of the NaZn<sub>13</sub> alloy during the sodiation process.</p>
         
         <p>The modulated Zn-diamane not only can manipulate the sodiophilicity of the separator to affect the Na ion flux, but also affects the interfacial chemistry of the Na metal anode, especially the SEI layer. The chemical composition of the SEI layer was analyzed by in-depth XPS analysis (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5f–h</a>). The anode obtained from the Na metal anodes disassembled from the Na||Zn-diamane/PP||Na symmetric battery after 30 cycles at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. The C 1s, O 1s, and F 1s signals exhibit progressive changes with varying etching depths of 0, 5, 15, and 35 nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5f–h</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5f</a>, in the C 1s spectrum, C─C (284.4 eV), C─O (285.1 eV), and C═O (288.9 eV), which are attributed to the organic species in the SEI layer, are gradually reduced with increasing the etching depth up to 35 nm.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0069" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0069_R_d5601348e1375" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 69 - Nanoscale">69</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the O 1s spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5g</a>), the peaks at 533.7 eV (C─O) and 530.8 eV (C═O) are consistent with those in the C 1s spectrum, while the peaks at 535.5 and 530 eV correspond to Na-KLL and Na<sub>2</sub>O, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0076" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0076_R_d5601348e1385" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 76 - ACS Nano">76</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The inorganic species, such as NaF (683.9 eV) and Na<sub>2</sub>O (530 eV) peaks increase with the etching depth up to 35 nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5g,h</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0077" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0077_R_d5601348e1396" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 77 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">77</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These results suggest that a beneficial NaF inorganic-rich inner layer of SEI is formed on the Na metal anodes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information). This inorganic-rich inner SEI layer and organic-rich outer SEI layer can effectively protect the sodium metal anodes with robust mechanical strength and high stability, which agrees well with the previous studies.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202417809-bib-0078" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202417809-bib-0078_R_d5601348e1405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 78 - Energy Storage Mater.">78</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the SEI layers of Na metal anodes disassembled from the Na||PP||Na and Na||GF/D||Na symmetric battery have more organics (such as C─C, C─O, and C═O) in inner SEI (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>The schematic representation of the stable Na metal deposition process utilizing the Zn-diamane modulated separator is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0005">5i</a>. Specifically, the Zn-diamane/PP separator, owing to the high sodiophilicity originated from the diamane coupled with the in-situ formed NaZn<sub>13</sub> alloy on the surface of the separator, can efficiently attract Na ions, facilitating a uniform Na ion flux across the separator and thereby fostering even Na deposition. Moreover, the Zn-diamane coating layer can improve Young's modulus of the separator to depress the dendrites to avoid the rupture of the separator. In addition, the Zn-diamane layer enhances the thermal diffusion rate and thermal stability. The Zn-diamane layer could efficiently mitigate the emergence of high-temperature induced hotspots, thereby establishing a homogeneous thermal environment for uniform Na ion flux and deposition. Furthermore, the homogeneous deposition process is instrumental in fostering an inorganic-rich inner layer and an organic-rich outer layer within the SEI layer, which serves as an effective barrier, shielding the Na metal anodes from electrolytic corrosion, thereby achieving the longevity and stability of Na metal anodes over extended cycles.</p>
         
         <p>To substantiate the practical viability of the modulated separator, a full SMB was evaluated by matching the NVP@C cathode and Na metal anode with the Zn-diamane/PP separator (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0006">6a</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0006">6b,c</a>, the full cell demonstrates superior rate performance. Specifically, the full cell with Zn-diamane/PP separator could deliver attractive capacities of 90, 90, 88, 85, 80, and 70 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 10, 20, 50, 100, 200, and 500 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The long cycle measurement shows that the full cell with the Zn-diamane separator can deliver a high capacity of 90 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, and maintain impressive capacity retention as high as 99% over 500 cycles with a minimal capacity decay of 0.003% per cycle, accompanied by a high average Coulombic efficiency of 99% at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0006">6d</a>). The charge/discharge curves at 1st, 100th, and 500th are very well overlapped, indicating the long cycle stability of the cell employing the Zn-diamane/PP separators (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0006">6e</a>). In contrast, cells with a PP separator can only keep capacity retentions of 51% over 200 cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information). To show the advances of the Zn-diamane/PP separator for the full cell, we compare the long cycling performance of SMB full cells with representative separators as shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). The dedicated NVP@C||Zn-diamane/PP||Na full cell exhibits long-cycle stability with the lowest capacity decay. Furthermore, to show the scalability of Zn-diamane/PP separators for larger-scale battery applications, a full SMB pouch cell was assembled with the size of 3.5 × 2.5 cm. This pouch cell can deliver a high capacity of 57.5 at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 98% even after 200 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202417809-fig-0006">6f,g</a>). In addition, to show the flexibility of the SMB pouch cell for the application of wearable electronics, another pouch cell with the size of 6 × 2 cm was also demonstrated. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a> (Supporting Information), the pouch cell with Zn-diamane/PP separator is capable of powering an LED and a small fan even under a bent configuration, underscoring its adaptability and utility in flexible electronic systems.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202417809-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6652f6f7-1f5c-4d31-ae0d-19a2bcd343dd/adfm202417809-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/6652f6f7-1f5c-4d31-ae0d-19a2bcd343dd/adfm202417809-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/fdc07c2e-eef2-43fd-ae6f-98e658c4ab6e/adfm202417809-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6652f6f7-1f5c-4d31-ae0d-19a2bcd343dd/adfm202417809-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202417809-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202417809" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance evaluation of the NVP@C||Zn-diamane/PP||Na full cell. a) Schematic illustration of the full cell. b) Rate performance measured at the current densities ranging from 10 to 500 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and c) corresponding GCD curves. d) Long cycling performance at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup> (activated with 20 mA g<sup>−1</sup> for the first 5 cycles), and e) corresponding GCD curves. f) Long cycling performance of the pouch cell at 100 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, and g) corresponding GCD curves at various cycles.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202417809-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202417809-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a Zn-diamane/PP separator was successfully designed and fabricated to manipulate the Na ion distribution and deposition. With this design, the Zn-diamane/PP separator could greatly promote Na<sup>+</sup> ion transfer number, electrolyte penetration and thermal stability. Upon cycling, the symmetric Na cell with Zn-diamane/PP separator could stably operate for more than 5000 h at 1 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>. Even at an ultra-high current density of 25 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>, the cell could still maintain a long lifespan of &gt;1000 h. The excellent long-cycle stability and high rate capability can be attributed to the high sodiophilicity enabled dendrite-free deposition morphology, uniform flux, and fast surface kinetics. The high sodiophilicity is originated from the diamane nanoflakes and in-situ formed NaZn<sub>13</sub> alloy during the initial discharge process. Finally, a full cell employing the Zn-diamane/PP separator can deliver a high capacity of 90 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 99% after 500 cycles. Our work provides new insights into modified separator strategies that are expected to be widely applied in SMBs and large-scale clean energy storage technology.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
